See below to configure test IP versions.\n   337→\n   338→## Linking against libc++ on Linux\n   339→\n   340→To link Envoy against libc++, follow the [quick start](#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers) to setup Clang+LLVM and run:\n   341→```\n   342→bazel build --config=libc++ envoy\n   343→```\n   344→\n   345→Or use our configuration with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, pass `--config=remote-clang-libc++` or\n   346→`--config=docker-clang-libc++` respectively.\n   347→\n   348→If you want to make libc++ as default, add a line `build --config=libc++` to the `user.bazelrc` file in Envoy source root.\n   349→\n   350→## Using a compiler toolchain in a non-standard location\n   351→\n   352→By setting the `CC` and `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` in the environment that Bazel executes from as\n   353→appropriate, an arbitrary compiler toolchain and standard library location can be specified. One\n   354→slight caveat is that (at the time of writing), Bazel expects the binutils in `$(dirname $CC)` to be\n   355→unprefixed, e.g. `as` instead of `x86_64-linux-gnu-as`.\n   356→\n   357→Note: this configuration currently doesn't work with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, you have to generate a\n   358→custom toolchains configuration for them. See [bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains)\n   359→for more details.\n   360→\n   361→## Supported compiler versions\n   362→\n   363→We now require Clang >= 9 due to C++17 support and tcmalloc requirement. GCC >= 9 is also known to work.\n   364→Currently the CI is running with Clang 14.\n   365→\n   366→## Clang STL debug symbols\n   367→\n   368→By default Clang drops some debug symbols that are required for pretty printing to work correctly.\n   369→More information can be found [here](https://bugs.llvm.org/show_bug.cgi?id=24202). The easy solution\n   370→is to set ```--copt=-fno-limit-debug-info``` on the CLI or in your .bazelrc file.\n   371→\n   372→## Removing debug info\n   373→\n   374→If you don't want your debug or release binaries to contain debug info\n   375→to reduce binary size, pass `--define=no_debug_info=1` when building.\n   376→This is primarily useful when building envoy as a static library. When\n   377→building a linked envoy binary you can build the implicit `.stripped`\n   378→target from [`cc_binary`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/be/c-cpp.html#cc_binary)\n   379→or pass [`--strip=always`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html#flag--strip)\n   380→instead.\n   381→\n   382→# Running the built Envoy binary on the host system\n   383→\n   384→After Envoy is built, it can be executed via CLI.\n   385→\n   386→For example, if Envoy was built using the `bazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static` command, then it can be executed from the project's root directory by running:\n   387→\n   388→```console\n   389→$(bazel info bazel-genfiles)/source/exe/envoy-static --config-path /path/to/your/envoy/config.yaml\n   390→```\n   391→\n   392→# Testing Envoy with Bazel\n   393→\n   394→All the Envoy tests can be built and run with:\n   395→\n   396→```\n   397→bazel test //test/...\n   398→```\n   399→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. See below to configure test IP versions.\n\n## Linking against libc++ on Linux\n\nTo link Envoy against libc++, follow the [quick start](#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers) to setup Clang+LLVM and run:\n```\nbazel build --config=libc++ envoy\n```\n\nOr use our configuration with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, pass `--config=remote-clang-libc++` or\n`--config=docker-clang-libc++` respectively.\n\nIf you want to make libc++ as default, add a line `build --config=libc++` to the `user.bazelrc` file in Envoy source root.\n\n## Using a compiler toolchain in a non-standard location\n\nBy setting the `CC` and `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` in the environment that Bazel executes from as\nappropriate, an arbitrary compiler toolchain and standard library location can be specified. One\nslight caveat is that (at the time of writing), Bazel expects the binutils in `$(dirname $CC)` to be\nunprefixed, e.g. `as` instead of `x86_64-linux-gnu-as`.\n\nNote: this configuration currently doesn't work with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, you have to generate a\ncustom toolchains configuration for them. See [bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains)\nfor more details.\n\n## Supported compiler versions\n\nWe now require Clang >= 9 due to C++17 support and tcmalloc requirement. GCC >= 9 is also known to work.\nCurrently the CI is running with Clang 14.\n\n## Clang STL debug symbols\n\nBy default Clang drops some debug symbols that are required for pretty printing to work correctly.\nMore information can be found [here](https://bugs.llvm.org/show_bug.cgi?id=24202). The easy solution\nis to set ```--copt=-fno-limit-debug-info``` on the CLI or in your .bazelrc file.\n\n## Removing debug info\n\nIf you don't want your debug or release binaries to contain debug info\nto reduce binary size, pass `--define=no_debug_info=1` when building.\nThis is primarily useful when building envoy as a static library. When\nbuilding a linked envoy binary you can build the implicit `.stripped`\ntarget from [`cc_binary`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/be/c-cpp.html#cc_binary)\nor pass [`--strip=always`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html#flag--strip)\ninstead.\n\n# Running the built Envoy binary on the host system\n\nAfter Envoy is built, it can be executed via CLI.\n\nFor example, if Envoy was built using the `bazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static` command, then it can be executed from the project's root directory by running:\n\n```console\n$(bazel info bazel-genfiles)/source/exe/envoy-static --config-path /path/to/your/envoy/config.yaml\n```\n\n# Testing Envoy with Bazel\n\nAll the Envoy tests can be built and run with:\n\n```\nbazel test //test/...\n```\n","numLines":200,"startLine":200,"totalLines":974}}}

For\nexample, for extremely verbose test debugging:\n\n```\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --test_arg=\"-l trace\"\n```\n\nBy default, testing exercises both IPv4 and IPv6 address connections. For other mode options, see the gperftools\nheap checker [documentation](https://gperftools.github.io/gperftools/heap_checker.html). To force it to rerun tests:\n\n```\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --cache_test_results=no\n```\n\nBazel will by default run all tests inside a sandbox, which disallows access to the\nlocal filesystem. If you need to break out of the sandbox (for example to run under a\nlocal script or tool with [`--run_under`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/user-manual.html#flag--run_under)),\nyou can run the test with `--strategy=TestRunner=local`, e.g.:\n\n```\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --strategy=TestRunner=local --run_under=/some/path/foobar.sh\n```\n# Stack trace symbol resolution\n\nEnvoy can produce backtraces on demand and from assertions and other fatal\nactions like segfaults. Where supported, stack traces will contain resolved\nsymbols, though not include line numbers. On systems where absl::Symbolization is\nnot supported, the stack traces written in the log or to stderr contain addresses rather\nthan resolved symbols. If the symbols were resolved, the address is also included at\nthe end of the line.\n\nThe `tools/stack_decode.py` script exists to process the output and do additional symbol\nresolution including file names and line numbers. It requires the `addr2line` program be\ninstalled and in your path. Any log lines not relevant to the backtrace capability are\npassed through the script unchanged (it acts like a filter). File and line information\nis appended to the stack trace lines.\n\nThe script runs in one of two modes. To process log input from stdin, pass `-s` as the first\nargument, followed by the executable file path. You can postprocess a log or pipe the output\nof an Envoy process. If you do not specify the `-s` argument it runs the arguments as a child\nprocess. This enables you to run a test with backtrace post processing. Bazel sandboxing must\nbe disabled by specifying local execution. Example command line with\n`run_under`:\n\n```\nbazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test\n--run_under=//tools:stack_decode --strategy=TestRunner=local\n--cache_test_results=no --test_output=all\n```\n\nExample using input on stdin:\n\n```\nbazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test --cache_test_results=no --test_output=streamed |& tools/stack_decode.py -s bazel-bin/test/server/backtrace_test\n```\n\nYou will need to use either a `dbg` build type or the `opt` build type to get file and line\nsymbol information in the binaries.\n\nBy default main.cc will install signal handlers to print backtraces at the\nlocation where a fatal signal occurred. The signal handler will re-raise the\nfatal signal with the default handler so a core file will still be dumped after\nthe stack trace is logged. To inhibit this behavior use\n`--define=signal_trace=disabled` on the Bazel command line. No signal handlers will\nbe installed.\n\n# Running a single Bazel test under GDB\n\n```\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test.dwp\ngdb bazel-bin/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test\n```\n\nWe need to use `-c dbg` Bazel option to generate debugging symbols and without\nthat GDB will not be very useful. The debugging symbols are stored as separate\ndebugging information files (`.dwp` files) and we can build a DWARF package file\nwith `.dwp ` target. The `.dwp` file need to be presented in the same folder with the\nbinary for a full debugging experience.\n\n# Running Bazel tests requiring privileges\n\nSome tests may require privileges (e.g. CAP_NET_ADMIN) in order to execute. One option is to run\nthem with elevated privileges, e.g. `sudo test`. However, that may not always be possible,\nparticularly if the test needs to run in a CI pipeline. `tools/bazel-test-docker.sh` may be used in\nsuch situations to run the tests in a privileged docker container.\n\nThe script works by wrapping the test execution in the current repository's circle ci build\ncontainer, then executing it either locally or on a remote docker container. In both cases, the\ncontainer runs with the `--privileged` flag, allowing it to execute operations which would otherwise\nbe restricted.\n\nThe command line format is:\n`tools/bazel-test-docker.sh <bazel-test-target> [optional-flags-to-bazel]`\n\nThe script uses two optional environment variables to control its behaviour:\n\n* `RUN_REMOTE=<yes|no>`: chooses whether to run on a remote docker server.\n* `LOCAL_MOUNT=<yes|no>`: copy/mount local libraries onto the docker container.\n\nUse `RUN_REMOTE=yes` when you don't want to run against your local docker instance. Note that you\nwill need to override a few environment variables to set up the remote docker. The list of variables\ncan be found in the [Documentation](https://docs.docker.com/engine/reference/commandline/cli/).\n\nUse `LOCAL_MOUNT=yes` when you are not building with the Envoy build container. This will ensure\nthat the libraries against which the tests dynamically link will be available and of the correct\nversion.\n\n## Examples\n\nRunning the http integration test in a privileged container:\n","numLines":150,"startLine":400,"totalLines":974}}}

There are existing tests which send requests with bodies, have\n    42→downstream or upstream disconnect or time out, send multiple simultaneous requests on the same\n    43→connection, etc. Given that many of the disconnect/timeout cases are covered, a common case for\n    44→testing is covering a newly added configuration option.\n    45→\n    46→Most of Envoy's tests have been migrated from using [`json flatfiles`](../config/integration/) to\n    47→using a basic configuration defined as `basic_config` in [`config/utility.cc`](../config/utility.cc).\n    48→This configuration may be modified before the call to `initialize()`.\n    49→The [`ConfigHelper`](../config/utility.h) has utilities for common alterations such as:\n    50→\n    51→```c++\n    52→// Set the default protocol to HTTP2\n    53→setDownstreamProtocol(Http::CodecType::HTTP2);\n    54→```\n    55→\n    56→or\n    57→\n    58→```c++\n    59→// Add a buffering filter on the request path\n    60→config_helper_.prependFilter(ConfigHelper::DEFAULT_BUFFER_FILTER);\n    61→```\n    62→\n    63→For other edits which are less likely reusable, one can add config modifiers. Config modifiers\n    64→allow arbitrary modification of Envoy’s configuration just before Envoy is brought up. One can add\n    65→a config modifier to alter the bootstrap proto, one which affects the first `HttpConnectionManager`\n    66→object in the config, or mix and match. Config modifiers are operated on in the order they are\n    67→added, so one could, for example, modify the default `HttpConnectionManager`, duplicate the listening\n    68→config, and then change the first `HttpConnectionManager` to be different from the second.\n    69→\n    70→An example of modifying the bootstrap proto to overwrite runtime defaults:\n    71→\n    72→```c++\n    73→config_helper_.addRuntimeOverride(\"Foo\", \"bar\");\n    74→});\n    75→```\n    76→\n    77→An example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to change Envoy’s HTTP/1.1 processing:\n    78→\n    79→```c++\n    80→config_helper_.addConfigModifier([&](envoy::extensions::filters::network::http_connection_manager::v3::HttpConnectionManager& hcm) -> void {\n    81→  nvoy::config::core::v3::Http1ProtocolOptions options;\n    82→  options.mutable_allow_absolute_url()->set_value(true);\n    83→  hcm.mutable_http_protocol_options()->CopyFrom(options);\n    84→};);\n    85→```\n    86→\n    87→An example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to add an additional upstream\n    88→cluster:\n    89→\n    90→```c++\n    91→   config_helper_.addConfigModifier([](envoy::config::bootstrap::v3::Bootstrap& bootstrap) {\n    92→      bootstrap.mutable_rate_limit_service()->set_cluster_name(\"ratelimit\");\n    93→      auto* ratelimit_cluster = bootstrap.mutable_static_resources()->add_clusters();\n    94→      ratelimit_cluster->MergeFrom(bootstrap.static_resources().clusters()[0]);\n    95→      ratelimit_cluster->set_name(\"ratelimit\");\n    96→      ConfigHelper::setHttp2(*ratelimit_cluster);\n    97→    });\n    98→```\n    99→\n   100→In addition to the existing test framework, which allows for carefully timed interaction and ordering of events between downstream, Envoy, and Upstream, there is now an “autonomous” framework which simplifies the common case where the timing is not essential (or bidirectional streaming is desired). When AutonomousUpstream is used, by setting `autonomous_upstream_ = true` before `initialize()`, upstream will by default create AutonomousHttpConnections for each incoming connection and AutonomousStreams for each incoming stream. In the common case, one\n\n- Sends a request from downstream through Envoy\n- Verifies the request is received upstream, and possibly inspects elements of the headers or body\n- Sends a response from upstream through Envoy\n- Verifies the request is received downstream, again possibly inspecting headers and body\n\nFor the simplest variant of this, one could do the following.\n\n```c++\n// start Envoy, set up the fake upstreams.\ninitialize();\n\n// Create a client aimed at Envoy’s default HTTP port.\ncodec_client_ = makeHttpConnection(makeClientConnection((lookupPort(\"http\"))));\n\n// Create some request headers.\nHttp::TestRequestHeaderMapImpl request_headers{{\":method\", \"GET\"},\n                                               {\":path\", \"/test/long/url\"},\n                                               {\":scheme\", \"http\"},\n                                               {\":authority\", \"host\"}};\n\n// Send the request headers from the client, wait until they are received upstream. When they\n// are received, send the default response headers from upstream and wait until they are\n// received at by client\nauto response = sendRequestAndWaitForResponse(request_headers, 0, default_response_headers_, 0);\n\n// Verify the proxied request was received upstream, as expected.\nEXPECT_TRUE(upstream_request_->complete());\nEXPECT_EQ(0U, upstream_request_->bodyLength());\n// Verify the proxied response was received downstream, as expected.\nEXPECT_TRUE(response->complete());\nEXPECT_STREQ(\"200\", response->headers().Status()->value().c_str());\nEXPECT_EQ(0U, response_->body().size());\n```\n\nOnce you have the basic end-to-end test, it is fairly straight forward to modify it to test more\ninteresting corner cases. There are existing tests which send requests with bodies, have\ndownstream or upstream disconnect or time out, send multiple simultaneous requests on the same\nconnection, etc. Given that many of the disconnect/timeout cases are covered, a common case for\ntesting is covering a newly added configuration option.\n\nMost of Envoy's tests have been migrated from using [`json flatfiles`](../config/integration/) to\nusing a basic configuration defined as `basic_config` in [`config/utility.cc`](../config/utility.cc).\nThis configuration may be modified before the call to `initialize()`.\nThe [`ConfigHelper`](../config/utility.h) has utilities for common alterations such as:\n\n```c++\n// Set the default protocol to HTTP2\nsetDownstreamProtocol(Http::CodecType::HTTP2);\n```\n\nor\n\n```c++\n// Add a buffering filter on the request path\nconfig_helper_.prependFilter(ConfigHelper::DEFAULT_BUFFER_FILTER);\n```\n\nFor other edits which are less likely reusable, one can add config modifiers. Config modifiers\nallow arbitrary modification of Envoy’s configuration just before Envoy is brought up. One can add\na config modifier to alter the bootstrap proto, one which affects the first `HttpConnectionManager`\nobject in the config, or mix and match. Config modifiers are operated on in the order they are\nadded, so one could, for example, modify the default `HttpConnectionManager`, duplicate the listening\nconfig, and then change the first `HttpConnectionManager` to be different from the second.\n\nAn example of modifying the bootstrap proto to overwrite runtime defaults:\n\n```c++\nconfig_helper_.addRuntimeOverride(\"Foo\", \"bar\");\n});\n```\n\nAn example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to change Envoy’s HTTP/1.1 processing:\n\n```c++\nconfig_helper_.addConfigModifier([&](envoy::extensions::filters::network::http_connection_manager::v3::HttpConnectionManager& hcm) -> void {\n  nvoy::config::core::v3::Http1ProtocolOptions options;\n  options.mutable_allow_absolute_url()->set_value(true);\n  hcm.mutable_http_protocol_options()->CopyFrom(options);\n};);\n```\n\nAn example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to add an additional upstream\ncluster:\n\n```c++\n   config_helper_.addConfigModifier([](envoy::config::bootstrap::v3::Bootstrap& bootstrap) {\n      bootstrap.mutable_rate_limit_service()->set_cluster_name(\"ratelimit\");\n      auto* ratelimit_cluster = bootstrap.mutable_static_resources()->add_clusters();\n      ratelimit_cluster->MergeFrom(bootstrap.static_resources().clusters()[0]);\n      ratelimit_cluster->set_name(\"ratelimit\");\n      ConfigHelper::setHttp2(*ratelimit_cluster);\n    });\n```\n\nIn addition to the existing test framework, which allows for carefully timed interaction and ordering of events between downstream, Envoy, and Upstream, there is now an “autonomous” framework which simplifies the common case where the timing is not essential (or bidirectional streaming is desired). When AutonomousUpstream is used, by setting `autonomous_upstream_ = true` before `initialize()`, upstream will by default create AutonomousHttpConnections for each incoming connection and AutonomousStreams for each incoming stream. By default, the streams will respond to each complete request with “200 OK” and 10 bytes of payload, but this behavior can be altered by setting various request headers, as documented in [`autonomous_upstream.h`](autonomous_upstream.h)","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":188}}}

Build Prerequisites\n\n### System Dependencies\n\nBefore building Envoy, you must install platform-specific dependencies:\n\n#### Ubuntu/Debian\n```bash\nsudo apt-get install \\\n   autoconf \\\n   curl \\\n   libtool \\\n   patch \\\n   python3-pip \\\n   unzip \\\n   virtualenv\n```\n\n#### Fedora/RHEL\n```bash\ndnf install \\\n    aspell-en \\\n    libatomic \\\n    libstdc++ \\\n    libstdc++-static \\\n    libtool \\\n    lld \\\n    patch \\\n    python3-pip\n```\n\n#### macOS\n```bash\nbrew install coreutils wget libtool go bazelisk clang-format autoconf aspell\n```\n- Requires full Xcode (not just Command Line Tools)\n- Tested with Apple clang version 11.0.0 or later\n\n#### Windows\n- Windows 10 SDK version 1903 (10.0.18362.1) or later\n- Visual Studio 2019 Build Tools with VC++ workload\n- Python 3 (from python.org, not MSYS2)\n- Git\n- MSYS2\n\n### Compiler Requirements\n\n- **Clang**: Version 9 or later (CI uses Clang 14)\n- **GCC**: Version 9 or later\n- **C++17 support**: Required\n\n### Build Tools\n\n1. **Bazelisk** (recommended instead of Bazel to avoid version conflicts)\n   - Linux: `sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\") && sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel`\n   - macOS: `brew install bazelisk`\n   - Windows: Download from GitHub releases and add to PATH\n\n2. **Go** (version 1.17 or later) - Required for BoringSSL and Buildifier\n\n3. **Buildifier and Buildozer** - For formatting Bazel BUILD files\n   ```bash\n   go install github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools/buildifier@latest\n   go install github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools/buildozer@latest\n   ```\n\n### Optional Setup: Development Support Toolchain\n\nInstall git hooks for automatic DCO signoff and pre-commit/pre-push checks:\n```bash\n./support/bootstrap\n```\n\nThis sets up:\n- Automatic DCO (Developer Certificate of Origin) signoff on commits\n- Format checking on push\n- Can be bypassed with `git commit --no-verify` if needed\n\n**Documentation**: See `support/README.md`\n\n---\n\n## 2. Build System\n\nEnvoy uses **Bazel** as its build system. Bazel is a fast, scalable build system that supports building and testing large codebases efficiently.\n\n### Key Build Commands\n\n#### Basic Build (debug/development)\n```bash\n# Build main Envoy binary\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with fastbuild (unoptimized, faster builds)\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy -c fastbuild\n\n# Build with optimization (release)\nbazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with debug symbols\nbazel build -c dbg //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build entire Envoy (including all extensions)\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy-static\n```\n\n#### Building Specific Components\n```bash\n# Build only a specific filter\nbazel build //source/extensions/filters/http/router:config_lib\n\n# Build a library for a subsystem\nbazel build //source/common/http:...\n\n# Use ... to build all targets in a directory\nbazel build //source/common/...\n```\n\n#### Compiler Configuration\n```bash\n# Build with libc++ (recommended for official releases)\nbazel build --config=libc++ //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with libstdc++\nbazel build --config=clang //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with GCC\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy  # default without --config=clang\n\n# Use Clang specifically\nbazel build --config=clang //source/exe:envoy\n```\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended for First-Time Setup)\nAvoids environment issues and ensures consistency with CI:\n```bash\n# Build development version using Docker\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n\n# Build release version\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\n\n# Build debug version\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\n```\n\nOutput locations:\n- Dev build: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild`\n- Release: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy`\n- Debug: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug`\n\nYou can change output directory: `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'`\n\n### Build Profiles\n\n- **fastbuild** (`-c fastbuild`): Unoptimized, minimal symbols, fastest compilation\n- **opt** (`-c opt`): Full optimization, minimal debug info, suitable for release\n- **dbg** (`-c dbg`): Unoptimized, full debug symbols, suitable for debugging with GDB\n\n### Getting Build Info\n```bash\n# Find the built binary path\nbazel info bazel-genfiles\n\n# Run the built binary\n$(bazel info bazel-genfiles)/source/exe/envoy --config-path /path/to/config.yaml\n```\n\n### Bazel Configuration Files\n\n- **Main config**: `.bazelrc` in repository root\n- **User overrides**: `user.bazelrc` in repository root (not tracked by git)\n- **Clang setup**: `clang.bazelrc` (generated by `bazel/setup_clang.sh`)\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nEnvoy uses the **Google Test** (gtest) framework with Google Mock for unit tests and a custom integration test framework.\n\n### Test Structure\n\n- **Unit tests**: Located in `test/` directories matching source structure\n  - Example: source code in `source/common/http/` has tests in `test/common/http/`\n  - Use Google Test framework with custom matchers\n- **Integration tests**: Located in `test/integration/`\n  - End-to-end testing with fake downstream/upstream servers\n  - Test real Envoy server code behavior\n- **Test frameworks**:\n  - Google Test + Google Mock for unit tests\n  - Custom `HttpIntegrationTest` framework for integration tests\n\n### Running Tests\n\n#### All Tests\n```bash\n# Run all tests\nbazel test //test/...\n\n# Run with verbose output\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/...\n```\n\n#### Specific Test Targets\n```bash\n# Run a single test file\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Run tests matching a pattern\nbazel test //test/common/http/...\n\n# Run tests in specific subsystem\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/router:...\n```\n\n#### With Additional Options\n```bash\n# Verbose test output\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Pass arguments to test binary\nbazel test --test_arg=\"-l trace\" //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Skip cache, rerun even if passed before\nbazel test --cache_test_results=no //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Test with IPv4 only\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v4only\n\n# Test with IPv6 only\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v6only\n```\n\n#### Coverage Builds\n```bash\n# Generate coverage report (requires specific setup)\nbazel test --config=coverage //test/...\n\n# Coverage build must achieve 100% for new code (validated in CI)\n```\n\n### Testing with Docker\n```bash\n# Run all tests in Docker (matches CI environment)\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh test'\n```\n\n### Heap Checking\nBy default, tests run with gperftools heap checker in \"normal\" mode:\n```bash\n# Disable heap checker\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=\n\n# Use minimal mode instead\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=minimal\n```\n\n### Integration Test Helpers\n\n**Location**: `test/integration/`\n\nKey classes:\n- `HttpIntegrationTest`: Base class for HTTP integration tests\n- `AutonomousUpstream`: Automatically responds to requests (useful for simple tests)\n- `ConfigHelper`: Utilities for modifying Envoy configuration in tests\n\nExample test structure:\n```cpp\n// Initialize Envoy with default config\ninitialize();\n\n// Create client connection\ncodec_client_ = makeHttpConnection(makeClientConnection((lookupPort(\"http\"))));\n\n// Create request and send it\nHttp::TestRequestHeaderMapImpl request_headers{...};\nauto response = sendRequestAndWaitForResponse(request_headers, 0, ...);\n\n// Verify results\nEXPECT_TRUE(response->complete());\n```\n\nSee `test/integration/README.md` for detailed integration test documentation.\n\n### Debugging Tests\n```bash\n# Build test binary with debug symbols\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test.dwp\n\n# Debug with GDB\ngdb bazel-bin/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test\n```\n\n### Custom Test Matchers\n\nEnvoy provides custom Google Mock matchers:\n- `HeaderValueOf(key, value)`: Check header values\n- `HttpStatusIs(status)`: Check HTTP status\n- `ProtoEq(proto)`: Compare protobuf messages\n- `HeaderMapEqual` / `HeaderMapEqualRef`: Compare header maps\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\nEnvoy uses multiple CI systems that automatically test all pull requests:\n\n### CI Platforms\n\n1. **Azure Pipelines** (Primary)\n   - Main CI platform\n   - Runs on all PR submissions\n   - **URL**: https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/\n\n2. **BazelCI**\n   - Runs remote execution tests\n   - Tests on Ubuntu 2004\n   - Tests: `//test/common/common/...`, `//test/integration/...`, `//test/exe/...`\n\n3. **Fuzz Testing**\n   - OSS-Fuzz continuous fuzzing\n   - **Badge**: Shown in README.md\n\n4. **Architecture-Specific CI**\n   - ppc64le builds (Jenkins: powerci.osuosl.org)\n   - s390x builds (Jenkins: ibmz-ci.osuosl.org)\n\n### CI Configuration Files\n\n- **Main CI config**: `.azure-pipelines/` directory\n- **BazelCI config**: `.bazelci/presubmit.yml`\n- **Script runners**: `ci/do_ci.sh`, `ci/run_envoy_docker.sh`\n- **Build setup**: `ci/build_setup.sh`\n- **Docker images**: See `ci/README.md`\n\n### Checks That Run on PRs\n\nThe CI pipeline validates:\n1. **Build**: Compilation with various configurations (Clang, GCC)\n2. **Unit Tests**: All Google Test tests pass\n3. **Integration Tests**: End-to-end tests pass\n4. **Code Format**: `clang-format` compliance (enforced by `.clang-tidy`)\n5. **Code Analysis**: `clang-tidy` linter checks\n6. **Coverage**: New code must have 100% test coverage\n7. **Documentation**: Markdown and RST validation\n8. **API**: Protocol buffer changes validated against API checklist\n\n### Typical CI Run Duration\n\n- Standard PR tests: **1-3 hours**\n- Full coverage build: **2-4 hours**\n- Release builds: **Varies by configuration**\n\n### Docker Build Images\n\n- **Ubuntu**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` (Ubuntu 20.04, GCC 9, Clang 14)\n- **Alpine**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-alpine` (minimal image)\n- **Windows**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` (Note: Windows support ended Aug 2023, patches accepted)\n\nGet image hash: `cat ci/envoy_build_sha.sh`\n\n### Rerunning CI Without Code Changes\n\n```bash\n# Rerun failed tasks only\n# Comment on PR with:\n/retest\n\n# Rerun all checks (empty commit push)\ngit commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI'\ngit push\n\n# Or use git alias:\ngit config --add alias.kick-ci '!git commit -s --allow-empty -m \"Kick CI\" && git push'\ngit kick-ci\n```\n\n### CI Environment Variables\n\n- `ENVOY_RBE`: Use remote execution\n- `ENVOY_STDLIB`: Choose `libstdc++` or `libc++` (default: `libc++`)\n- `IMAGE_NAME`: Choose Docker image (default: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`)\n- `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`: Force Docker image refresh\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Before Starting Work\n\n1. **Check GitHub Issues**\n   - Search for existing issues related to your change\n   - Check if someone is already working on it\n\n2. **For Major Features**\n   - Create a GitHub issue for discussion\n   - **Major** = > 100 lines of code (excluding tests) OR changes user-facing behavior\n   - Discuss design and get maintainer agreement before implementing\n   - Prevents wasted effort and ensures architectural alignment\n\n3. **For Small Bugs and Fixes**\n   - No prior communication needed\n   - Just submit the PR\n\n4. **For Extensions**\n   - Read **EXTENSION_POLICY.md** for extension addition policy\n   - Review **GOVERNANCE.md** for extension guidelines\n\n**Documentation**: `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `PULL_REQUESTS.md`, `EXTENSION_POLICY.md`\n\n### Contribution Requirements\n\nEvery PR must satisfy:\n\n1. **100% Test Coverage**\n   - All new code must be covered by tests\n   - Can verify with coverage build\n   - If coverage impossible, explain why in PR description\n\n2. **Documentation**\n   - Changes to user-facing behavior require docs in `docs/` directory\n   - API changes documented inline with protos\n   - Release notes added to `changelogs/current.yaml` for user-impacting changes\n\n3. **DCO Sign-off**\n   - Every commit must be signed off: `Signed-off-by: Your Name <email@example.com>`\n   - Set up automatic signoff: `./support/bootstrap`\n   - Or use `git commit -s`\n\n4. **Code Style**\n   - Follow **STYLE.md** guidelines\n   - Code formatted with `clang-format` (automatically checked by CI)\n   - Follow Google C++ style guide with Envoy deviations:\n     - Function names: `camelCase` starting with lowercase (e.g., `doFoo()`)\n     - Member variables: postfix `_` (e.g., `foo_`)\n     - Enums: PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`)\n     - Line limit: 100 columns\n     - Include guards: `#pragma once`\n\n5. **Inclusive Language**\n   - No \"whitelist\" → use \"allowlist\"\n   - No \"blacklist\" → use \"denylist\" or \"blocklist\"\n   - No \"master\" → use \"primary\" or \"main\"\n   - No \"slave\" → use \"secondary\" or \"replica\"\n\n6. **Tests Must Pass**\n   - All existing tests must continue to pass\n   - New tests must pass\n   - CI must be green before merge\n\n### Submitting a PR\n\n1. **Fork the repository** on GitHub\n\n2. **Create a feature branch**\n   ```bash\n   git checkout -b my-feature\n   ```\n\n3. **Install git hooks**\n   ```bash\n   ./support/bootstrap\n   ```\n   This provides:\n   - Automatic DCO signoff\n   - Pre-push format checking\n\n4. **Implement your changes**\n   - Add tests\n   - Run tests locally: `bazel test //test/...`\n   - Run format checks: `bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix`\n\n5. **Commit with DCO signoff**\n   ```bash\n   git commit -s -m \"subsystem: brief description\"\n   ```\n   Example messages:\n   - `\"docs: fix grammar error\"`\n   - `\"http conn man: add new feature\"`\n   - `\"router: fix bug in retry logic\"`\n\n6. **Create Pull Request**\n   - Use descriptive title (starts with subsystem)\n   - Provide detailed commit message explaining what and why\n   - Include PR description with sections:\n     - **Risk**: Low | Medium | High\n     - **Testing**: What testing was done\n     - **Documentation**: Changes to docs/API or \"N/A\"\n     - **Release Notes**: Add to `changelogs/current.yaml` if user-impacting\n     - **Fixes**: Link to issues (e.g., \"Fixes #1234\")\n   - Use PR template: `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`\n\n7. **Address Review Feedback**\n   - **DO NOT rebase** after review starts (forces reviewer to re-review)\n   - **DO NOT force-push** (use `git merge main` instead to pull latest changes)\n   - Push new commits to address feedback\n   - Re-request review after addressing comments\n\n### Code Review Expectations\n\n- **Review turnaround**: Typically within 1 business day\n- **Reviewers**:\n  - Senior maintainer for core code\n  - Domain expert for specific areas\n  - At least one approver from different organization for new extensions\n- **Merge process**: Maintainer will squash-rebase and merge when approved\n  - Final commit message cleaned up before merge\n  - DCO signoff preserved\n\n### PR Fields to Complete\n\n**Title**: `subsystem: brief description`\n- Lowercase for both subsystem and description\n- Examples: `\"http conn man: add new feature\"`, `\"router: fix x-envoy-overloaded header\"`\n\n**Commit Message**: Explains what and why\n- Used as final commit message when merged\n- Document behavior before/after if applicable\n- Note configuration options if any\n\n**Additional Description**: Context for reviewers\n- Can include information beyond commit message scope\n- References to related discussions or issues\n\n**Risk Level**:\n- **Low**: Small bug fix or small optional feature\n- **Medium**: New features, small-medium changes to existing components\n- **High**: Complex changes, flow control, critical component rewrites\n\n**Testing**: Describe testing performed\n- Unit tests, integration tests, manual testing\n- Higher risk = more comprehensive testing expected\n\n**Documentation**: Describe doc changes\n- Write \"N/A\" if no docs changes\n- Include inline proto docs for API changes\n- Update \"Life of a Request\" if structural dataplane changes\n\n**Release Notes**: Add entry to `changelogs/current.yaml`\n- Required if user-impacting OR extension-impacting\n- Include relevant documentation links\n- Format: See existing examples in changelog\n\n**Platform-Specific Features**: If applicable\n- Explain OS-specific socket options\n- Create tracking issues for platforms not supported\n- Avoid `#ifdef OSNAME`, use feature guards\n\n**Runtime Guard**: If needed\n- Add for user-visible behavioral changes\n- Document in release notes and PR description\n- See CONTRIBUTING.md runtime guarding section\n\n### Special Cases\n\n**Deprecations**:\n- Update `changelogs/current.yaml` deprecated section\n- Deprecation script will create cleanup issue in next release\n- Note specific deprecation in commit message\n\n**API Changes**:\n- Review API Review Checklist: `api/review_checklist.md`\n- Document API considerations in PR\n- Changes to `api/` tree require special review\n\n**Runtime Guards**:\n- For high-risk behavioral changes\n- Keep both old and new code paths\n- Default to new behavior after testing period\n- Remove old path after deprecation window\n\n### Repository Etiquette\n\n- Push to personal fork, not main Envoy repo (keeps it lean)\n- Use branches in fork for feature branches\n- Avoid rebasing after review starts\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\nThis example walks through implementing a bug fix to the HTTP connection manager filter.\n\n### Step 1: Prepare Your Environment\n\n```bash\n# Clone the repository\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n\n# Set up git hooks for DCO and format checking\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Install Bazel/Bazelisk if not already installed\nsudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-amd64\nsudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel\n```\n\n### Step 2: Identify the Issue\n\nSuppose you want to fix a bug in the HTTP connection manager filter that's causing it to incorrectly handle timeout values.\n\n```bash\n# Find related code\ngrep -r \"timeout\" source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/ | grep -i bug\n\n# Look at the filter structure\nls -la source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\n```\n\n### Step 3: Create a Feature Branch\n\n```bash\ngit checkout -b fix-http-conn-man-timeout\n```\n\n### Step 4: Write Tests First\n\nCreate a test file to demonstrate the bug:\n```bash\n# Find existing test file for the component\nls test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\n\n# Open the test file and add a test case that fails with current code\nvim test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager_test.cc\n```\n\nExample test structure:\n```cpp\n// test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager_test.cc\nTEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerTest, TimeoutBugFix) {\n  // Setup config with timeout value\n  setupBasicConfig();\n  config_helper_.addRuntimeOverride(\"envoy.http.timeout\", \"5000\");\n\n  initialize();\n\n  // Create connection and verify timeout behavior\n  codec_client_ = makeHttpConnection(...);\n\n  // Verify fix: timeout should be applied correctly\n  EXPECT_EQ(5000U, conn_manager_->getTimeout());\n}\n```\n\n### Step 5: Run the Failing Test\n\n```bash\n# Build and run your new test\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:http_connection_manager_test \\\n  --test_arg=\"--gtest_filter=HttpConnectionManagerTest.TimeoutBugFix\" \\\n  --test_output=streamed\n\n# Should fail with current code\n```\n\n### Step 6: Implement the Fix\n\nLocate and fix the bug in the implementation:\n```bash\n# Find the implementation file\nvim source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager.cc\n\n# Make the fix to handle timeout values correctly\n```\n\n### Step 7: Verify the Fix\n\n```bash\n# Run just the test you fixed\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:http_connection_manager_test \\\n  --test_arg=\"--gtest_filter=HttpConnectionManagerTest.TimeoutBugFix\" \\\n  --test_output=streamed\n\n# Should now pass\n\n# Run all tests for the http_connection_manager to ensure no regressions\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:...\n\n# Run a broader set of integration tests\nbazel test //test/integration:... -k \"http\"\n```\n\n### Step 8: Verify Code Style and Format\n\n```bash\n# Fix code formatting automatically\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Run clang-tidy checks\nbazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main\n\n# Or in Docker if you don't have the tools installed locally\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n```\n\n### Step 9: Add Documentation and Release Notes\n\n```bash\n# If this bug fix affects user-facing behavior, add release notes\nvim changelogs/current.yaml\n```\n\nExample entry:\n```yaml\n- area: http_conn_man\n  change: |\n      fixed: Corrected timeout handling in HTTP connection manager filter to properly apply\n      configured timeout values. Previously timeout values were incorrectly parsed and could\n      cause connections to timeout prematurely. See #1234.\n```\n\n```bash\n# If there's user-facing documentation, update it\nvim docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/http_connection_manager.rst\n```\n\n### Step 10: Commit Your Changes\n\n```bash\n# Stage your changes\ngit add source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager.cc\ngit add test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager_test.cc\ngit add changelogs/current.yaml\ngit add docs/root/configuration/...\n\n# Commit with DCO signoff (./support/bootstrap adds the hook for this)\ngit commit -s -m \"http conn man: fix timeout value handling\n\nThis fixes a bug where timeout values in the HTTP connection manager filter\nwere not being correctly parsed, causing connections to timeout prematurely.\n\nPreviously:\n- Timeout values were passed directly without validation\n- Integer overflow could occur on edge cases\n\nNow:\n- Timeout values are properly validated and sanitized\n- Edge cases are handled correctly\n\nFixes #1234\"\n\n# Git hook will automatically add your DCO signoff\n```\n\n### Step 11: Create a Pull Request\n\n```bash\n# Push your branch to your fork\ngit push origin fix-http-conn-man-timeout\n```\n\nThen on GitHub:\n1. Click \"Create Pull Request\"\n2. Fill in the PR template:\n   - **Title**: `\"http conn man: fix timeout value handling\"`\n   - **Risk Level**: `Low` (bug fix)\n   - **Testing**: `\"Added unit test TestTimeoutBugFix to verify timeout values are properly handled. Ran full http_connection_manager test suite. Verified no regressions with integration tests.\"`\n   - **Documentation**: `\"Updated changelogs/current.yaml with fix description. No API changes.\"`\n   - **Release Notes**: Added to `changelogs/current.yaml`\n   - **Fixes**: `\"Fixes #1234\"`\n\n### Step 12: Address Review Feedback\n\nWhen a maintainer reviews your PR:\n\n```bash\n# Make requested changes\nvim source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager.cc\n\n# Verify tests still pass\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:...\n\n# Commit the fix (don't rebase!)\ngit commit -s -m \"Address review feedback: improve error message clarity\"\n\n# Push the new commit\ngit push origin fix-http-conn-man-timeout\n\n# The maintainer will see just the new changes, not re-review the whole PR\n```\n\n### Step 13: Merge\n\nOnce all checks pass (CI tests turn green) and a maintainer approves:\n1. Maintainer will squash-merge your PR\n2. Your commits are squashed into one\n3. Commit message is cleaned up if needed\n4. Your DCO signoff is preserved\n5. Change is now in main branch\n\n### Step 14: Verify on Main\n\n```bash\n# Update your local repo\ngit checkout main\ngit pull\n\n# Verify your change is there\ngit log --oneline | grep \"timeout value handling\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n### Official Documentation\n- **Envoy Official Docs**: https://www.envoyproxy.io/\n- **Build Documentation**: `bazel/README.md`, **Integration Test Framework**: `test/integration/README.md`\n\n---\n\n## Quick Reference: Common Commands\n\n```bash\n# Set up development environment\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Build main binary\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with optimization\nbazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Run all unit tests\nbazel test //test/...\n\n# Run specific test\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --test_output=streamed\n\n# Fix code formatting\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Run Docker build (matches CI environment)\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n\n# Create commit with automatic DCO signoff\ngit commit -s -m \"subsystem: description\"\n\n# Rerun CI without code changes\ngit commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\n```\n\n---\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Build Issues\n\n**Clang not found**:\n- Install from `bazel/setup_clang.sh` or specify compiler: `bazel build --config=clang //source/exe:envoy`\n\n**Long paths error on Windows**:\n- Set `startup --output_base=C:/_eb` in `.bazelrc` to shorten Bazel paths\n\n**Out of disk space**:\n- Bazel can use significant disk space. Clean with `bazel clean`\n\n### Test Failures\n\n**Flaky tests**:\n- Rerun with `--cache_test_results=no`\n- Use simulated time in tests instead of real time\n\n**Heap check failures**:\n- Disable with `--test_env=HEAPCHECK=` or switch mode: `--test_env=HEAPCHECK=minimal`\n\n**Tests timing out**:\n- Run with more verbose output to debug: `--test_output=streamed`\n- Check system load and resources\n\n### Git/DCO Issues\n\n**DCO signature missing**:\n- Re-run `./support/bootstrap` to set up hooks\n- Or manually add: `git commit -s` or `git commit --amend -s`\n\n**Can't push (pre-push hook failing)**:\n- Check format with `bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix`\n- Or bypass with `git push --no-verify` (not recommended)\n\n---\n\nLast Updated: March 2026\nBased on Envoy v1.32.1 and main branch\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1123,"cache_read_input_tokens":62382,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1123},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1ede1b77-cfd3-43e9-9325-2deb3f5d0ec2","uuid":"204f85cb-368a-469d-b671-4be5f5a939a9"}

Build Prerequisites\n\n### System Dependencies\n\nBefore building Envoy, you must install platform-specific dependencies:\n\n#### Ubuntu/Debian\n```bash\nsudo apt-get install \\\n   autoconf \\\n   curl \\\n   libtool \\\n   patch \\\n   python3-pip \\\n   unzip \\\n   virtualenv\n```\n\n#### Fedora/RHEL\n```bash\ndnf install \\\n    aspell-en \\\n    libatomic \\\n    libstdc++ \\\n    libstdc++-static \\\n    libtool \\\n    lld \\\n    patch \\\n    python3-pip\n```\n\n#### macOS\n```bash\nbrew install coreutils wget libtool go bazelisk clang-format autoconf aspell\n```\n- Requires full Xcode (not just Command Line Tools)\n- Tested with Apple clang version 11.0.0 or later\n\n#### Windows\n- Windows 10 SDK version 1903 (10.0.18362.1) or later\n- Visual Studio 2019 Build Tools with VC++ workload\n- Python 3 (from python.org, not MSYS2)\n- Git\n- MSYS2\n\n### Compiler Requirements\n\n- **Clang**: Version 9 or later (CI uses Clang 14)\n- **GCC**: Version 9 or later\n- **C++17 support**: Required\n\n### Build Tools\n\n1. **Bazelisk** (recommended instead of Bazel to avoid version conflicts)\n   - Linux: `sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\") && sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel`\n   - macOS: `brew install bazelisk`\n   - Windows: Download from GitHub releases and add to PATH\n\n2. **Go** (version 1.17 or later) - Required for BoringSSL and Buildifier\n\n3. **Buildifier and Buildozer** - For formatting Bazel BUILD files\n   ```bash\n   go install github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools/buildifier@latest\n   go install github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools/buildozer@latest\n   ```\n\n### Optional Setup: Development Support Toolchain\n\nInstall git hooks for automatic DCO signoff and pre-commit/pre-push checks:\n```bash\n./support/bootstrap\n```\n\nThis sets up:\n- Automatic DCO (Developer Certificate of Origin) signoff on commits\n- Format checking on push\n- Can be bypassed with `git commit --no-verify` if needed\n\n**Documentation**: See `support/README.md`\n\n---\n\n## 2. Build System\n\nEnvoy uses **Bazel** as its build system. Bazel is a fast, scalable build system that supports building and testing large codebases efficiently.\n\n### Key Build Commands\n\n#### Basic Build (debug/development)\n```bash\n# Build main Envoy binary\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with fastbuild (unoptimized, faster builds)\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy -c fastbuild\n\n# Build with optimization (release)\nbazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with debug symbols\nbazel build -c dbg //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build entire Envoy (including all extensions)\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy-static\n```\n\n#### Building Specific Components\n```bash\n# Build only a specific filter\nbazel build //source/extensions/filters/http/router:config_lib\n\n# Build a library for a subsystem\nbazel build //source/common/http:...\n\n# Use ... to build all targets in a directory\nbazel build //source/common/...\n```\n\n#### Compiler Configuration\n```bash\n# Build with libc++ (recommended for official releases)\nbazel build --config=libc++ //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with libstdc++\nbazel build --config=clang //source/exe:envoy\n\n# Build with GCC\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy  # default without --config=clang\n\n# Use Clang specifically\nbazel build --config=clang //source/exe:envoy\n```\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended for First-Time Setup)\nAvoids environment issues and ensures consistency with CI:\n```bash\n# Build development version using Docker\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n\n# Build release version\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\n\n# Build debug version\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\n```\n\nOutput locations:\n- Dev build: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild`\n- Release: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy`\n- Debug: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug`\n\nYou can change output directory: `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'`\n\n### Build Profiles\n\n- **fastbuild** (`-c fastbuild`): Unoptimized, minimal symbols, fastest compilation\n- **opt** (`-c opt`): Full optimization, minimal debug info, suitable for release\n- **dbg** (`-c dbg`): Unoptimized, full debug symbols, suitable for debugging with GDB\n\n### Getting Build Info\n```bash\n# Find the built binary path\nbazel info bazel-genfiles\n\n# Run the built binary\n$(bazel info bazel-genfiles)/source/exe/envoy --config-path /path/to/config.yaml\n```\n\n### Bazel Configuration Files\n\n- **Main config**: `.bazelrc` in repository root\n- **User overrides**: `user.bazelrc` in repository root (not tracked by git)\n- **Clang setup**: `clang.bazelrc` (generated by `bazel/setup_clang.sh`)\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nEnvoy uses the **Google Test** (gtest) framework with Google Mock for unit tests and a custom integration test framework.\n\n### Test Structure\n\n- **Unit tests**: Located in `test/` directories matching source structure\n  - Example: source code in `source/common/http/` has tests in `test/common/http/`\n  - Use Google Test framework with custom matchers\n- **Integration tests**: Located in `test/integration/`\n  - End-to-end testing with fake downstream/upstream servers\n  - Test real Envoy server code behavior\n- **Test frameworks**:\n  - Google Test + Google Mock for unit tests\n  - Custom `HttpIntegrationTest` framework for integration tests\n\n### Running Tests\n\n#### All Tests\n```bash\n# Run all tests\nbazel test //test/...\n\n# Run with verbose output\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/...\n```\n\n#### Specific Test Targets\n```bash\n# Run a single test file\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Run tests matching a pattern\nbazel test //test/common/http/...\n\n# Run tests in specific subsystem\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/router:...\n```\n\n#### With Additional Options\n```bash\n# Verbose test output\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Pass arguments to test binary\nbazel test --test_arg=\"-l trace\" //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Skip cache, rerun even if passed before\nbazel test --cache_test_results=no //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Test with IPv4 only\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v4only\n\n# Test with IPv6 only\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v6only\n```\n\n#### Coverage Builds\n```bash\n# Generate coverage report (requires specific setup)\nbazel test --config=coverage //test/...\n\n# Coverage build must achieve 100% for new code (validated in CI)\n```\n\n### Testing with Docker\n```bash\n# Run all tests in Docker (matches CI environment)\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh test'\n```\n\n### Heap Checking\nBy default, tests run with gperftools heap checker in \"normal\" mode:\n```bash\n# Disable heap checker\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=\n\n# Use minimal mode instead\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=minimal\n```\n\n### Integration Test Helpers\n\n**Location**: `test/integration/`\n\nKey classes:\n- `HttpIntegrationTest`: Base class for HTTP integration tests\n- `AutonomousUpstream`: Automatically responds to requests (useful for simple tests)\n- `ConfigHelper`: Utilities for modifying Envoy configuration in tests\n\nExample test structure:\n```cpp\n// Initialize Envoy with default config\ninitialize();\n\n// Create client connection\ncodec_client_ = makeHttpConnection(makeClientConnection((lookupPort(\"http\"))));\n\n// Create request and send it\nHttp::TestRequestHeaderMapImpl request_headers{...};\nauto response = sendRequestAndWaitForResponse(request_headers, 0, ...);\n\n// Verify results\nEXPECT_TRUE(response->complete());\n```\n\nSee `test/integration/README.md` for detailed integration test documentation.\n\n### Debugging Tests\n```bash\n# Build test binary with debug symbols\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test.dwp\n\n# Debug with GDB\ngdb bazel-bin/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test\n```\n\n### Custom Test Matchers\n\nEnvoy provides custom Google Mock matchers:\n- `HeaderValueOf(key, value)`: Check header values\n- `HttpStatusIs(status)`: Check HTTP status\n- `ProtoEq(proto)`: Compare protobuf messages\n- `HeaderMapEqual` / `HeaderMapEqualRef`: Compare header maps\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\nEnvoy uses multiple CI systems that automatically test all pull requests:\n\n### CI Platforms\n\n1. **Azure Pipelines** (Primary)\n   - Main CI platform\n   - Runs on all PR submissions\n   - **URL**: https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/\n\n2. **BazelCI**\n   - Runs remote execution tests\n   - Tests on Ubuntu 2004\n   - Tests: `//test/common/common/...`, `//test/integration/...`, `//test/exe/...`\n\n3. **Fuzz Testing**\n   - OSS-Fuzz continuous fuzzing\n   - **Badge**: Shown in README.md\n\n4. **Architecture-Specific CI**\n   - ppc64le builds (Jenkins: powerci.osuosl.org)\n   - s390x builds (Jenkins: ibmz-ci.osuosl.org)\n\n### CI Configuration Files\n\n- **Main CI config**: `.azure-pipelines/` directory\n- **BazelCI config**: `.bazelci/presubmit.yml`\n- **Script runners**: `ci/do_ci.sh`, `ci/run_envoy_docker.sh`\n- **Build setup**: `ci/build_setup.sh`\n- **Docker images**: See `ci/README.md`\n\n### Checks That Run on PRs\n\nThe CI pipeline validates:\n1. **Build**: Compilation with various configurations (Clang, GCC)\n2. **Unit Tests**: All Google Test tests pass\n3. **Integration Tests**: End-to-end tests pass\n4. **Code Format**: `clang-format` compliance (enforced by `.clang-tidy`)\n5. **Code Analysis**: `clang-tidy` linter checks\n6. **Coverage**: New code must have 100% test coverage\n7. **Documentation**: Markdown and RST validation\n8. **API**: Protocol buffer changes validated against API checklist\n\n### Typical CI Run Duration\n\n- Standard PR tests: **1-3 hours**\n- Full coverage build: **2-4 hours**\n- Release builds: **Varies by configuration**\n\n### Docker Build Images\n\n- **Ubuntu**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` (Ubuntu 20.04, GCC 9, Clang 14)\n- **Alpine**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-alpine` (minimal image)\n- **Windows**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` (Note: Windows support ended Aug 2023, patches accepted)\n\nGet image hash: `cat ci/envoy_build_sha.sh`\n\n### Rerunning CI Without Code Changes\n\n```bash\n# Rerun failed tasks only\n# Comment on PR with:\n/retest\n\n# Rerun all checks (empty commit push)\ngit commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI'\ngit push\n\n# Or use git alias:\ngit config --add alias.kick-ci '!git commit -s --allow-empty -m \"Kick CI\" && git push'\ngit kick-ci\n```\n\n### CI Environment Variables\n\n- `ENVOY_RBE`: Use remote execution\n- `ENVOY_STDLIB`: Choose `libstdc++` or `libc++` (default: `libc++`)\n- `IMAGE_NAME`: Choose Docker image (default: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`)\n- `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`: Force Docker image refresh\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Before Starting Work\n\n1. **Check GitHub Issues**\n   - Search for existing issues related to your change\n   - Check if someone is already working on it\n\n2. **For Major Features**\n   - Create a GitHub issue for discussion\n   - **Major** = > 100 lines of code (excluding tests) OR changes user-facing behavior\n   - Discuss design and get maintainer agreement before implementing\n   - Prevents wasted effort and ensures architectural alignment\n\n3. **For Small Bugs and Fixes**\n   - No prior communication needed\n   - Just submit the PR\n\n4. **For Extensions**\n   - Read **EXTENSION_POLICY.md** for extension addition policy\n   - Review **GOVERNANCE.md** for extension guidelines\n\n**Documentation**: `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `PULL_REQUESTS.md`, `EXTENSION_POLICY.md`\n\n### Contribution Requirements\n\nEvery PR must satisfy:\n\n1. **100% Test Coverage**\n   - All new code must be covered by tests\n   - Can verify with coverage build\n   - If coverage impossible, explain why in PR description\n\n2. **Documentation**\n   - Changes to user-facing behavior require docs in `docs/` directory\n   - API changes documented inline with protos\n   - Release notes added to `changelogs/current.yaml` for user-impacting changes\n\n3. **DCO Sign-off**\n   - Every commit must be signed off: `Signed-off-by: Your Name <email@example.com>`\n   - Set up automatic signoff: `./support/bootstrap`\n   - Or use `git commit -s`\n\n4. **Code Style**\n   - Follow **STYLE.md** guidelines\n   - Code formatted with `clang-format` (automatically checked by CI)\n   - Follow Google C++ style guide with Envoy deviations:\n     - Function names: `camelCase` starting with lowercase (e.g., `doFoo()`)\n     - Member variables: postfix `_` (e.g., `foo_`)\n     - Enums: PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`)\n     - Line limit: 100 columns\n     - Include guards: `#pragma once`\n\n5. **Inclusive Language**\n   - No \"whitelist\" → use \"allowlist\"\n   - No \"blacklist\" → use \"denylist\" or \"blocklist\"\n   - No \"master\" → use \"primary\" or \"main\"\n   - No \"slave\" → use \"secondary\" or \"replica\"\n\n6. **Tests Must Pass**\n   - All existing tests must continue to pass\n   - New tests must pass\n   - CI must be green before merge\n\n### Submitting a PR\n\n1. **Fork the repository** on GitHub\n\n2. **Create a feature branch**\n   ```bash\n   git checkout -b my-feature\n   ```\n\n3. **Install git hooks**\n   ```bash\n   ./support/bootstrap\n   ```\n   This provides:\n   - Automatic DCO signoff\n   - Pre-push format checking\n\n4. **Implement your changes**\n   - Add tests\n   - Run tests locally: `bazel test //test/...`\n   - Run format checks: `bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix`\n\n5. **Commit with DCO signoff**\n   ```bash\n   git commit -s -m \"subsystem: brief description\"\n   ```\n   Example messages:\n   - `\"docs: fix grammar error\"`\n   - `\"http conn man: add new feature\"`\n   - `\"router: fix bug in retry logic\"`\n\n6. **Create Pull Request**\n   - Use descriptive title (starts with subsystem)\n   - Provide detailed commit message explaining what and why\n   - Include PR description with sections:\n     - **Risk**: Low | Medium | High\n     - **Testing**: What testing was done\n     - **Documentation**: Changes to docs/API or \"N/A\"\n     - **Release Notes**: Add to `changelogs/current.yaml` if user-impacting\n     - **Fixes**: Link to issues (e.g., \"Fixes #1234\")\n   - Use PR template: `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`\n\n7. **Address Review Feedback**\n   - **DO NOT rebase** after review starts (forces reviewer to re-review)\n   - **DO NOT force-push** (use `git merge main` instead to pull latest changes)\n   - Push new commits to address feedback\n   - Re-request review after addressing comments\n\n### Code Review Expectations\n\n- **Review turnaround**: Typically within 1 business day\n- **Reviewers**:\n  - Senior maintainer for core code\n  - Domain expert for specific areas\n  - At least one approver from different organization for new extensions\n- **Merge process**: Maintainer will squash-rebase and merge when approved\n  - Final commit message cleaned up before merge\n  - DCO signoff preserved\n\n### PR Fields to Complete\n\n**Title**: `subsystem: brief description`\n- Lowercase for both subsystem and description\n- Examples: `\"http conn man: add new feature\"`, `\"router: fix x-envoy-overloaded header\"`\n\n**Commit Message**: Explains what and why\n- Used as final commit message when merged\n- Document behavior before/after if applicable\n- Note configuration options if any\n\n**Additional Description**: Context for reviewers\n- Can include information beyond commit message scope\n- References to related discussions or issues\n\n**Risk Level**:\n- **Low**: Small bug fix or small optional feature\n- **Medium**: New features, small-medium changes to existing components\n- **High**: Complex changes, flow control, critical component rewrites\n\n**Testing**: Describe testing performed\n- Unit tests, integration tests, manual testing\n- Higher risk = more comprehensive testing expected\n\n**Documentation**: Describe doc changes\n- Write \"N/A\" if no docs changes\n- Include inline proto docs for API changes\n- Update \"Life of a Request\" if structural dataplane changes\n\n**Release Notes**: Add entry to `changelogs/current.yaml`\n- Required if user-impacting OR extension-impacting\n- Include relevant documentation links\n- Format: See existing examples in changelog\n\n**Platform-Specific Features**: If applicable\n- Explain OS-specific socket options\n- Create tracking issues for platforms not supported\n- Avoid `#ifdef OSNAME`, use feature guards\n\n**Runtime Guard**: If needed\n- Add for user-visible behavioral changes\n- Document in release notes and PR description\n- See CONTRIBUTING.md runtime guarding section\n\n### Special Cases\n\n**Deprecations**:\n- Update `changelogs/current.yaml` deprecated section\n- Deprecation script will create cleanup issue in next release\n- Note specific deprecation in commit message\n\n**API Changes**:\n- Review API Review Checklist: `api/review_checklist.md`\n- Document API considerations in PR\n- Changes to `api/` tree require special review\n\n**Runtime Guards**:\n- For high-risk behavioral changes\n- Keep both old and new code paths\n- Default to new behavior after testing period\n- Remove old path after deprecation window\n\n### Repository Etiquette\n\n- Push to personal fork, not main Envoy repo (keeps it lean)\n- Use branches in fork for feature branches\n- Avoid rebasing after review starts\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\nThis example walks through implementing a bug fix to the HTTP connection manager filter.\n\n### Step 1: Prepare Your Environment\n\n```bash\n# Clone the repository\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n\n# Set up git hooks for DCO and format checking\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Install Bazel/Bazelisk if not already installed\nsudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-amd64\nsudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel\n```\n\n### Step 2: Identify the Issue\n\nSuppose you want to fix a bug in the HTTP connection manager filter that's causing it to incorrectly handle timeout values.\n\n```bash\n# Find related code\ngrep -r \"timeout\" source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/ | grep -i bug\n\n# Look at the filter structure\nls -la source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\n```\n\n### Step 3: Create a Feature Branch\n\n```bash\ngit checkout -b fix-http-conn-man-timeout\n```\n\n### Step 4: Write Tests First\n\nCreate a test file to demonstrate the bug:\n```bash\n# Find existing test file for the component\nls test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\n\n# Open the test file and add a test case that fails with current code\nvim test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager_test.cc\n```\n\nExample test structure:\n```cpp\n// test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager_test.cc\nTEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerTest, TimeoutBugFix) {\n  // Setup config with timeout value\n  setupBasicConfig();\n  config_helper_.addRuntimeOverride(\"envoy.http.timeout\", \"5000\");\n\n  initialize();\n\n  // Create connection and verify timeout behavior\n  codec_client_ = makeHttpConnection(...);\n\n  // Verify fix: timeout should be applied correctly\n  EXPECT_EQ(5000U, conn_manager_->getTimeout());\n}\n```\n\n### Step 5: Run the Failing Test\n\n```bash\n# Build and run your new test\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:http_connection_manager_test \\\n  --test_arg=\"--gtest_filter=HttpConnectionManagerTest.TimeoutBugFix\" \\\n  --test_output=streamed\n\n# Should fail with current code\n```\n\n### Step 6: Implement the Fix\n\nLocate and fix the bug in the implementation:\n```bash\n# Find the implementation file\nvim source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager.cc\n\n# Make the fix to handle timeout values correctly\n```\n\n### Step 7: Verify the Fix\n\n```bash\n# Run just the test you fixed\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:http_connection_manager_test \\\n  --test_arg=\"--gtest_filter=HttpConnectionManagerTest.TimeoutBugFix\" \\\n  --test_output=streamed\n\n# Should now pass\n\n# Run all tests for the http_connection_manager to ensure no regressions\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:...\n\n# Run a broader set of integration tests\nbazel test //test/integration:... -k \"http\"\n```\n\n### Step 8: Verify Code Style and Format\n\n```bash\n# Fix code formatting automatically\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Run clang-tidy checks\nbazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main\n\n# Or in Docker if you don't have the tools installed locally\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n```\n\n### Step 9: Add Documentation and Release Notes\n\n```bash\n# If this bug fix affects user-facing behavior, add release notes\nvim changelogs/current.yaml\n```\n\nExample entry:\n```yaml\n- area: http_conn_man\n  change: |\n      fixed: Corrected timeout handling in HTTP connection manager filter to properly apply\n      configured timeout values. Previously timeout values were incorrectly parsed and could\n      cause connections to timeout prematurely. See #1234.\n```\n\n```bash\n# If there's user-facing documentation, update it\nvim docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/http_connection_manager.rst\n```\n\n### Step 10: Commit Your Changes\n\n```bash\n# Stage your changes\ngit add source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager.cc\ngit add test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager_test.cc\ngit add changelogs/current.yaml\ngit add docs/root/configuration/...\n\n# Commit with DCO signoff (./support/bootstrap adds the hook for this)\ngit commit -s -m \"http conn man: fix timeout value handling\n\nThis fixes a bug where timeout values in the HTTP connection manager filter\nwere not being correctly parsed, causing connections to timeout prematurely.\n\nPreviously:\n- Timeout values were passed directly without validation\n- Integer overflow could occur on edge cases\n\nNow:\n- Timeout values are properly validated and sanitized\n- Edge cases are handled correctly\n\nFixes #1234\"\n\n# Git hook will automatically add your DCO signoff\n```\n\n### Step 11: Create a Pull Request\n\n```bash\n# Push your branch to your fork\ngit push origin fix-http-conn-man-timeout\n```\n\nThen on GitHub:\n1. Click \"Create Pull Request\"\n2. Fill in the PR template:\n   - **Title**: `\"http conn man: fix timeout value handling\"`\n   - **Risk Level**: `Low` (bug fix)\n   - **Testing**: `\"Added unit test TestTimeoutBugFix to verify timeout values are properly handled. Ran full http_connection_manager test suite. Verified no regressions with integration tests.\"`\n   - **Documentation**: `\"Updated changelogs/current.yaml with fix description. --config=clang //source/exe:envoy`\n\n**Long paths error on Windows**:\n- Set `startup --output_base=C:/_eb` in `.bazelrc` to shorten Bazel paths\n\n**Out of disk space**:\n- Bazel can use significant disk space. Clean with `bazel clean`\n\n### Test Failures\n\n**Flaky tests**:\n- Rerun with `--cache_test_results=no`\n- Use simulated time in tests instead of real time\n\n**Heap check failures**:\n- Disable with `--test_env=HEAPCHECK=` or switch mode: `--test_env=HEAPCHECK=minimal`\n\n**Tests timing out**:\n- Run with more verbose output to debug: `--test_output=streamed`\n- Check system load and resources\n\n### Git/DCO Issues\n\n**DCO signature missing**:\n- Re-run `./support/bootstrap` to set up hooks\n- Or manually add: `git commit -s` or `git commit --amend -s`\n\n**Can't push (pre-push hook failing)**:\n- Check format with `bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix`\n- Or bypass with `git push --no-verify` (not recommended)\n\n---\n\nLast Updated: March 2026\nBased on Envoy v1.32.1 and main branch\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
